  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d006aaa2-a7b5-474b-90fb-ae4ee9f7201e'
      });

  <span id="freeText7217490814494339089" style="display:none">When Edward Cullen and Bella Swan met in <i>Twilight</i>, an iconic love story was born. But until now, fans have heard only Bella's side of the story. At last, readers can experience Edward's version in the long-awaited companion novel, <i>Midnight Sun</i>.<br /><br />This unforgettable tale as told through Edward's eyes takes on a new and decidedly dark twist. Meeting Bella is both the most unnerving and intriguing event he has experienced in all his years as a vampire. As we learn more fascinating details about Edward's past and the complexity of his inner thoughts, we understand why this is the defining struggle of his life. How can he justify following his heart if it means leading Bella into danger?</span>

Thank you, Stephenie Meyer for presenting us at this difficult time. I believe it may be difficult to think about releasing the other books in the series, but is there a possibility?</a>

<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/68970862-chelsierra">ChelSierra</a>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent"> — I'm hoping that now that she has Edward back in her head, he will refuse to leave her brain until she finishes the whole series from his point of v<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent"> — I'm hoping that now that she has Edward back in her head, he will refuse to leave her brain until she finishes the whole series from his point of view. I really want the confrontation between the Cullens and the Volturi from Edward's POV.<br /><br />Plus, in New Moon, Edward was chasing Victoria all across the country, and lost her in Brazil. He didn't realize Victoria would head back to Forks to go after Bella. So, I'd like to know what he was thinking while in Brazil, and why he never ever considered that Bella might be in danger.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1820361-m-i-the-only-one-fearing-about-this">m I the only one fearing about this? 
Haven&#39;t re-read twilight in a while but let&#39;s be honest,those were books for teens and if they are trying to sell us the same story over again, with the same fifteen year old perspective,I think it isn&#39;t going to work. I mean,sure she knows we all grow up, and we are no longer got flushed with a few kissing scenes right? Do u believe this ll be darker n steamier?</a>
</div>

<ul class='questionFooterActions'>

<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1820361'><a id="like_count_community_question_1820361" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/1820361?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">22 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F53287484-midnight-sun">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/29162873-regina"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1559945117i/29162873._UY100_CR16,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/29162873-regina">Regina</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">If you've read the draft then you'll have found out that there's so much more information in it due to Edward not sleeping and being able to read mind<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">If you've read the draft then you'll have found out that there's so much more information in it due to Edward not sleeping and being able to read minds. In my view, it's going to be 1000x more times more interesting than Bella's POV. From the partial Midnight Sun draft alone we found out what happens to the men in Port Angeles, we never would've found out in Twilight because Edward never mentions it again.<br /><br />If you don't want to read the same story again, fair enough, but we're finally getting an internal monologue from Edward and we're going to be able to understand him much, much better. My Twilight copy is 434 pages long and Midnight Sun is at least 600/700 (where I ordered from says 752) so it'll reveal never known details about the original series.<br /><br />Obviously, I can't comment on whether she's changed anything major because it isn't out yet but she has mentioned that she was given the freedom to do whatever she wanted in the scenes without Bella. I do assume the internal monologue is going to be a big darker, though. What nerves me most is the direct quote from the description, "This unforgettable tale as told through Edward's eyes takes on a new and decidedly dark twist." so we’ll just have to wait and see what happens. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_3318000314" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3318000314" />
    <a title="Angelica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16201093-angelica"><img alt="Angelica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507050077p2/16201093.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3318000314?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angelica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angelica" href="/user/show/16201093-angelica">Angelica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=release-2020">release-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=read-2020">read-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=authors-i-love">authors-i-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3318000314" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17364337620944650244"><b>I have never in my 23 years of life been more excited to read a book and I am not ashamed! I loved reading this, but I didn't necessarily <i>love</i> this book. Bear with me, I will explain!</b><br/><br/>This book isn't perfect, and I didn't expect it to be. It has many of the major criticized flaws of <i>Twilight</i>, in terms of instalove and questionable romance.  <b>It is a <i>Twilight</i> novel after all, and if you're one of those people that absolutely hate sparkly vampires and all that comes with them, this is NOT the book f</b></span>
  <span id="freeText17364337620944650244" style="display:none"><b>I have never in my 23 years of life been more excited to read a book and I am not ashamed! I loved reading this, but I didn't necessarily <i>love</i> this book. Bear with me, I will explain!</b><br /><br />This book isn't perfect, and I didn't expect it to be. It has many of the major criticized flaws of <i>Twilight</i>, in terms of instalove and questionable romance.  <b>It is a <i>Twilight</i> novel after all, and if you're one of those people that absolutely hate sparkly vampires and all that comes with them, this is NOT the book for you.</b> This book was written for the Twihards. It was written for everyone that had been eagerly awaiting this installment for over a decade. For those of us who recognize <i>Twilight's</i> flaws, but love it nonetheless. So, if you know that you're going to hate it, don't read it for the lolz, and don't ruin it for those of us who care about it. Please. That's all I ask.<br /><br /><b>That said, <i>Midnight Sun</i> is 'technically' better than <i>Twilight</i>.</b> Meyer's prose has grown and greatly improved in the past 15 years since Twilight first came out. Many of us have laughed at infamous <i>Twilight</i> lines such as: <i>“Aro laughed. "Ha ha ha," he giggled.”</i><br /><br />(Which is a misquote, by the way. It's actually: <i>“Aro started to laugh. “Ha ha ha,” he chuckled.”</i> In New Moon, chapter 21. Look it up!)<br /><br />Thankfully, we've grown past that mess in <i>Midnight Sun</i>. The writing was, surprisingly, actually of my favorite parts of this book.<br /><br /><b>When it comes to plot, this is literally the same as <i>Twilight</i></b>. Don't go expecting a new story because you won't get one. What you will get is a new version of it with far more detail and development than we see in the original novel. Meyer took the opportunity in this book to expand and develop a lot of things that were left vague before, and I really appreciate that. The vampire world seems bigger here, the characters seem like they could possibly, with some effort, be real people!<br /><br /><b>Character-wise, I really liked this book and consider it a good contribution to the Twilight Saga. </b>I am extremely biased as I have always been #TeamEdward, but I genuinely enjoyed the look into Edward's thoughts. He is still a vampire stalker, but he is also shockingly self-aware and not nearly as perfect as Bella thinks. <b>Seeing him through Bella's POV made Edward seem distant and otherworldly and entirely without flaw. Seeing his own mind shows he's a flawed, complex mess of a person. It makes him a bit more human than before.</b><br /><br />Shockingly, the biggest surprise for me in this book was Bella herself, as she too appears more human in this book than in <i>Twilight</i>. Don't get me wrong, <b>Bella is still the most special of all special snowflakes, but through Edward's eyes, you see she actually has a personality.</b> There are conversations between the two characters that are only alluded to and skipped over in <i>Twilight</i>, which were fully fleshed out in this book. Perhaps it's because, in <i>Twilight</i>, Bella was too infatuated with Edward to pay attention to small, trivial conversations. In <i>Midnight Sun</i>, Edward is so infatuated with Bella that he considers all those trivial conversations vital to her character. Either way, <b>Bella's personality, her likes, and dislikes, get explored here in a way that wasn't in the original novel. It makes her less bland.</b><br /><br />All the other characters are also shown in greater depth in this book, mostly, the Cullen clan. This is because Edward can read their minds and therefore see their true selves and hidden motives, while Bella's POV was blinded by their beauty and perceived perfection. Emmett was my favorite because he was the only one aware of the fact that Edward was clearly crazy.<br /><br />I will say this though, it sucks that all the human characters lowkey suck. I mean, they sucked in <i>Twilight</i> too, we just didn't realize how much. <b>All of Bella's "friends" are lying, jealous, horrible people and it sucks that Meyer chose to portray them like that for the sake of making Bella appear even more special.</b> Even Rosalie, who has a genuinely horrifying, tragic backstory of being used and abused and left for dead, is reduced to a horrible, jealous mean girl, and I didn't like that.<br /><br />In the end, this book was good and I highly recommend it to any <i>Twilight</i> fan. Keep in mind that this is literally the plot of the original <i>Twilight</i>. <b>Don't expect anything new or innovative, just a fresh perspective. That said, I promise you, this perspective will not disappoint.</b><br /><br /> <b>Still, I must admit, there were points in which the book felt overly long. </b> I kept waiting for certain things to happen and would get annoyed when I realized how early on in the story I still was, despite having read so many pages (this is a 658 page, 240k word novel). But,  I attribute this to knowing all the major plot points from <i>Twilight</i>. I was waiting for things to occur, waiting for my favorite scenes to come up and waiting, finally, for the action to happen.<br /><br /><b>It is one of the reasons why my rating cannot be higher than what I gave it. This book could never measure up to <i>Twilight</i> for me. My love for that book is based on an emotional attachment to the story rather than the quality or general readability of the novel. Unfortunately, I have no such attachment to this book. While I liked this book, I know that had this not been a <i>Twilight</i> novel, a part of the saga that I have loved for so long, I would not have found it nearly as enjoyable.</b><br /><br />And yet, having read this, I somehow feel complete. I have been waiting for this book for a decade, and I am so happy that I could finally get my hands on it. I can die happy in knowing that my last impression of <i>Twilight</i> wasn't that awful <i>Life and Death</i>, gender-bent nonsense. Seriously, <i>Life and Death</i> was a trash novel. <i>Midnight Sun</i>, on the other hand, was everything I expected it to be.<br /><br />#TeamEdward<br /><br />Follow Me Here Too:<b> <a href="http://www.thebookcovergirls.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">My Blog</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/covergirlreads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/book-cover-girl-19339391" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin'</a> || <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookcovergirls//" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://thebookcovergirls.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/thebookcovergirls/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="17364337620944650244" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48727754-chan?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48727754-chan?shelf=all-time-faves">all-time-faves</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3319503373" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15767152806683494622"><b>i would like to thank not only god but mormon jesus for bestowing this gift upon me in the year of our lord 2020<br/><br/>let's all stand for 672 pages of murderous, horny edward</b><br/><br/>---------------------------------------<br/><br/>review:<br/><br/>i had <b>no idea</b> going into this book what i wanted it to be. i read the original 12 leaked chapters back in the day and just like everyone else i craved an entire tome. but i am <b>so glad</b> that we didn't get the release 12 years ago. the wait was undoubtedly worth it.<br/><br/>this book delivered eve</span>
  <span id="freeText15767152806683494622" style="display:none"><b>i would like to thank not only god but mormon jesus for bestowing this gift upon me in the year of our lord 2020<br /><br />let's all stand for 672 pages of murderous, horny edward</b><br /><br />---------------------------------------<br /><br />review:<br /><br />i had <b>no idea</b> going into this book what i wanted it to be. i read the original 12 leaked chapters back in the day and just like everyone else i craved an entire tome. but i am <b>so glad</b> that we didn't get the release 12 years ago. the wait was undoubtedly worth it.<br /><br />this book delivered every unanswered question, every charming moment with side characters, every <b>aching</b> piece of internal dialogue from edward. we get to see edward at his most depraved, his most happy, his most anxious. we get to experience him falling in love. and it all made <b>so much sense.</b> if you find yourself wondering upon reread of twilight why the two fall so quickly, i feel like this book answers that question. and for all detractors of edward, i think we get a really convincing look at his attitude toward his relationship with bella (i.e. consent &amp; respect king).<br /><br /><b>in short, it was everything that a fan could hope for. my adoration for this book is without end. and my love for this series, much like edward's love for bella, is eternal.</b><br /><br />---------------------------------------<br /><br />also! if you love the twilight series, i think it's important to know that the real Quileute Tribe hasn't received any compensation from either Stephenie Meyer or the series/movies/merch (despite their culture and legends being misappropriated in the books). currently the Tribe is trying to move some of their buildings (such as their Tribal school) to higher ground because they are in a tsunami zone. here's a link to understand more/to donate!<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://mthg.org/">https://mthg.org/</a><br /></span>

<div id="review_3320064349" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3320064349" />
    <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell"><img alt="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584062476p2/2190064.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3320064349?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell">Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=kissing-books">kissing-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=ya-ya-land">ya-ya-land</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=pnr-uf">pnr-uf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3320064349" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18352882060163490161"><a href='https://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/alwaysbeebooked/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/>I was still a teenager when I first read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2561187623' rel='nofollow noopener'>TWILIGHT</a>, and now I am... well, <i>not </i>a teenager, obviously. (Beware, kiddos who follow me, one day, you too will be one of the "olds.") Since that first initial read, I've reread TWILIGHT a handful of times, and each time, I've felt a little differently about it as my thoughts about feminism, young adult fiction, and romances slowly changed and evolved with my own self-identification over time. I e</span>
  <span id="freeText18352882060163490161" style="display:none"><a href="https://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/alwaysbeebooked/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br>I was still a teenager when I first read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2561187623" rel="nofollow noopener">TWILIGHT</a>, and now I am... well, <i>not </i>a teenager, obviously. (Beware, kiddos who follow me, one day, you too will be one of the "olds.") Since that first initial read, I've reread TWILIGHT a handful of times, and each time, I've felt a little differently about it as my thoughts about feminism, young adult fiction, and romances slowly changed and evolved with my own self-identification over time. I eventually settled on a sort of affectionate resignation. No, TWILIGHT won't be winning any female empowerment awards, and it's all too easy to make fun of (whether it's vampire baseball, sparkling in the sunlight, or the infamous misuse of the word "nattering"). But it was a book written by a woman for young girls that somehow became overwhelmingly popular <i>and </i>a cultural phenomenon, and women really didn't get to have a lot of things like that. Most things in pop-culture are created by dudes, from the perspective of the male gaze, so it was refreshing to see a romance novel become so inescapably popular that it gained a firm toehold in the fantasy/paranormal literary canon <i>forever</i>.<br><br><br><br>Even if the heroine was a klutz with zero self-preservation.<br><br><br><br>I actually read the original version of MIDNIGHT SUN back when it was still available to read for free on Stephenie Meyer's website. I remember when she first announced the project, she got <i>so much backlash </i>for it, and everyone said she was greedy/milking the cash cow/etc. (and yet radio silence when every other romance author decided to copy her and write POVs from their own abusive heroes' perspectives). I remember there was a lot of drama because someone had leaked the chapters, and they were circulating the internet, and Meyer was mad and said something like, "I'm not going to write this anymore because if I did, I'd let James win and kill off all the Cullens!" And in a final "so there!" she had posted a PDF version of the leaked chapters on her own website. Which... yikes. Not yikes to Meyer but just yikes because I honestly felt so bad for her at the time, getting all that hate and then someone screwing her over like that. I'd probably want to red wedding my own characters, too, at that point. So I read the 12 chapters on Meyers' website and went on with my life...<br><br><br><br>Until our year of 2020 when Meyer announced to the world that she would FINALLY be publishing MIDNIGHT SUN, the rewrite that nobody asked for. Or... um, wait, actually I think LIFE AND DEATH was probably the rewrite that nobody asked for. Anyway, people took in this news and basically lumped in with the general craziness of 2020 but they also had Thoughts. I had Thoughts. Namely:<br><br><br><br>1. Ummm, okay, that's great and all but WHAT ABOUT THE HOST SEQUELS.<br><br>2. And why does that cover make me so uncomfortable? It looks soooo sexual.<br><br>3. There is no way that this is going to be good but I am a trash can-- we all know that I'm a trash can-- and TWILIGHT was my shit back in the day, so we all know I'm totes mcgoats reading this.<br><br>4. I REGRET NOTHING.<br><br>5. Does this mean that vampires are FINALLY becoming popular again?<br><br>6. Just kidding. That was a trick question because we all know vampires never left.<br><br><br><br>Anyway, I finally got my hands on this book and managed to read it in a day with some skimming and all I can say is HOLY HELL WHY AREN'T MORE PEOPLE TALKING ABOUT WHAT A CREEPS MCDEEPS EDWARD IS. Like, yikes. If you thought he was problematic and patriarchal in the firsts four books, grab a blowtorch and some mace, because he takes stalking and problematic behavior to serial killer heights. Where it's methodically breaking down how he would go about meticulously snapping the necks and killing everyone in his biology lab in order to get to Bella while her blood is still warm, or stealing what I believe was her house key (some kind of key) while sniffing her hair and then OILING HER WINDOW TO MAKE IT EASIER TO SNEAK INTO TO WATCH HER SLEEP, Edward is the King of Creepy. And what makes it worse is that he knows what he is doing is creepy and he literally does not care.<br><br><br><br>Another thing that I found really funny in this book is how Stephenie Meyer really tries to give us a reason as to (1) why every single heterosexual man with a functional penis pants after Bella in the books and (2) belatedly and retroactively tries to infuse her with a "personality." What results is that we are treated, through Edward's psychic powers, of the inner monologues of EVERY MAN in this book who finds Bella attractive and told over and over again how dazzling, how stunning she is that she leaves boys literally unable to think while speaking with her-- and she doesn't even know it! Bella dramatically understates her own worth and Edward finds this so charming, compelling, and appealing that he has taken it upon himself to act as appraiser. Which is... gross. But gross is a recurring theme in this book, just as another recurring theme in this book is every attractive woman who actually knows she's attractive being repeatedly looked down upon, rejected, and shamed.<br><br><br><br>Woo, feminism!<br><br><br><br>Through Edward's eyes, we're told how selfless and good Bella is. They have a conversation that definitely wasn't in the first book and felt about twenty pages long (I think it was actually ten) in which Edward asks Bella all of her favorite things, and she answers, so we learn her favorite flower (dahlia), candy (black licorice and sour patch-- is she an old lady??), and ALL OF HER FAVORITE BOOKS which we already kind of knew about from the previous four books, but now in addition to the Jane Eyres and Jane Austens, we're informed that she loves Robin McKinley and the Dragonriders of Pern series, and oh yes, Agatha Christie! She's BRANCHED OUT!<br><br><br><br>I must say, this book felt about a thousand times longer than it actually was. In addition to the long odes to Bella courtesy of Edward's being psychic, we're also treated to long and waxing odes of how rich, attractive, and amazing Edward is, courtesy of his being psychic. One creepy thing in this book which I'm really not seeing mentioned more in the reviews of this book is how Edward allegedly looks seventeen and yet a number of older women-- adult women-- in this book are panting after him and fantasizing over him, EVEN THOUGH HE IS A TEENAGER. I'm sorry, that's gross. That's just as gross as a one-hundred-and-four-year-old man panting after a teenager.<br><br><br><br>Which is another thing that makes this book creepy. Being inside Edward's head, we find out just how unequal their relationship is. Edward holds <i>two medical degrees </i>and is over a century old, and yet he doesn't like women of his own age and doesn't like women who have sexual agency (they seem to make him feel some weird mix of scorn and shame). Instead, he goes to a high school, where he sneers at the biology teacher for not knowing as much as he does with his ~sniff~ two medical degrees, and tunes in to his fellow "high school students" like he's watching a soap opera on the radio. Like... why?? If I was an immortal psychic vampire, high school is the literally last place I would go. I'd be on a remote island somewhere with my own personal library, or travel the world. I certainly would not be looking at lab slides and writing out prophase, anaphase, interphase.<br><br><br><br>TWILIGHT works because it's written (allegedly) from the perspective of a teenage girl who doesn't feel like she fits in, who feels like she's more mature for her peers, who feels like she sacrifices endlessly and nobody knows it and she doesn't want people to know it, but also she does. She whines about attention while craving it, and even though she's annoying, she is also a perfect stand-in for the walking, irrational paradox that many teenage girls (and boys, and people) are. It works. And how many of us, told that "things will get better in college" haven't innocently fantasized about a dashing older man (or woman) who would sweep us away from high school and tell us we're special and also a secret princess or heiress or faerie queen or whatever? Everyone wants to be special, especially people who are not. So, even though TWILIGHT doesn't really make sense, and Edward is ridiculous and toxic AF, the fantasy is appealing because it taps into Bella's desire to be seen and, yes, special.<br><br><br><br>MIDNIGHT SUN, however, doesn't work-- because it rips the sparkly tablecloth off that fantasy, revealing the horrors underneath. Edward is dangerous. He's a stalker, he's a bit of a psychopath, he has anger issues, he's jealous, he's possessive, and he's one-hundred-and-four years old and in love with a teenager, and because of that discrepancy, he feels like he knows what he wants better than she does-- because he's an adult, and she's the irrational, and naive teenager. In this book, it's no longer romantic; it's creepy. As we see Edward not through Bella's rosy lenses but through Edward's own, we realize just how creepy he is. So if this was an attempt to rationalize and humanize Edward's behaviors, it failed, because it only served to make him 10x creepier. But if this was Meyer's attempt to be like, "ha ha! you want dark?? I'll give you DARK," then she succeeded, because man, Edward is super scary and I want no part of him. Team Jacob all the way, thanks. At least he's her own age.<br><br><br><br>The only thing this book really succeeded at was filling in some of the bizarre plot holes from TWILIGHT, such as why the tracker didn't recognize what Bella was right away at the baseball game, and why, between Alice's mind-reading and Edward's psychic powers, Bella ended up having so much bad shit happen to her in this first book anyway. I didn't ask for MIDNIGHT SUN and I'm not really sure it adds anything of real value to the series, apart from doubling down on the Edward is Creepy vibes from the previous book while trying to ret-con Bella's vapid, schoolmarmish character based on criticism from the first four books. Only one of those things was successful, though, and I don't think it was the one that the author was going for, sadly.<br><br><br><br>1.5 to 2 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="18352882060163490161" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText14023006638004400609" style="display:none">This book is 1,800 pages long.<br /><br />I'm not fact-checking myself, but rest assured it feels in the foundational religious text/600-level STEM textbook range.<br /><br />And I read every one of those proverbial tissue-paper pages. (I did not actually read a hard copy of this. See below hinting.)<br /><br />And yet, I have exactly one note.<br /><br />That note is: <i>there is nothing funnier to me than charlie literally being no thoughts head empty. i knew i respected that man for a reason #acab</i><br /><br />Helpful? No. But it made me laugh. So thank you, past Emma.<br /><br />To be honest, I really liked this book at first. It almost...concerned me. It would have been devastating to my brand and image to genuinely enjoy a Twilight book in 2020.<br /><br />But thank god Stephenie Meyer saved me from herself.<br /><br />Because this got old very, very quickly.<br /><br />Twilight power rankings -<br />1) Alice<br />2) Charlie, the only cop I respect<br />3) Edward<br /><br />And yet this book still wasn't good.<br /><br />Being in Edward's head gets old. I can't imagine how he did it for 11,000 years before creeping on a child.<br /><br />But let's get out of here before we have to start considering the morals of this series.<br /><br />Bottom line: Don't - Read this book. Do - <a href="https://mthg.org/" rel="nofollow noopener">Donate to the Quileutes.</a><br /><br />----------<br /><br />well. i did it.<br /><br />but at what cost????<br /><br />review to come / 3 stars<br /><br />----------<br /><br />LET'S! GET! READY! TO! SUUUUUUUFFER!<br /><br /><i>note: this series is bad and has done a lot of damage. i donated what this book would have cost me to the <a href="https://mthg.org/" rel="nofollow noopener">Quileute tribe's move to higher ground</a> and paid $0 for this. let's leave it at that.</i><br /><br />----------<br /><br />what better way to spend a summer than by reading thousands of pages' worth of sexually frustrated vampires<br /><br />----------<br /><br />i already swallowed my pride and added the old edition of this book...now i have to do it again?!<br /><br />13 year old me better appreciate this</span>

<div id="review_3318049422" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3318049422" />
    <a title="Christy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11284813-christy"><img alt="Christy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594293998p2/11284813.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3318049422?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/11284813-christy">Christy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11284813-christy?shelf=2020-five-stars">2020-five-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11284813-christy?shelf=2020-ya-challenge">2020-ya-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11284813-christy?shelf=2020-audio">2020-audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3318049422" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15763710253844133084"><b>5 stars</b> <br/><br/><a href='https://app.photobucket.com/u/Christyb23/a/f189be23-9080-4c6a-a25f-26fbed1e07c6/p/0e65e2e4-0dbf-4025-88c4-26412f8705c5' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1597171425i/29950487._SY540_.png' alt='319C1FAC_8DCD_4A0C_BCB4_32CDA60BFD00_IMG_7980' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“For just a second, I saw Persephone, pomegranate in hand. Dooming herself to the underworld. Is that who I was? Hades himself, coveting springtime, stealing it, condemning it to endless night.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br/><i>Midnight Sun</i> is a book I’ve been waiting for for over 12 years and let me tell you, it was so worth the wait! I honestly thought this day would never come and as soon as I saw the book was available, I preordered the hardback for my collection and the audiobook. I listened to all 2</span>
  <span id="freeText15763710253844133084" style="display:none"><b>5 stars</b> <br><br><a href="https://app.photobucket.com/u/Christyb23/a/f189be23-9080-4c6a-a25f-26fbed1e07c6/p/0e65e2e4-0dbf-4025-88c4-26412f8705c5" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1597171425i/29950487._SY540_.png" alt="319C1FAC_8DCD_4A0C_BCB4_32CDA60BFD00_IMG_7980" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“For just a second, I saw Persephone, pomegranate in hand. Dooming herself to the underworld. Is that who I was? Hades himself, coveting springtime, stealing it, condemning it to endless night.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br><i>Midnight Sun</i> is a book I’ve been waiting for for over 12 years and let me tell you, it was so worth the wait! I honestly thought this day would never come and as soon as I saw the book was available, I preordered the hardback for my collection and the audiobook. I listened to all 25+ hours of this and the narration was AMAZING. Jake Abel did a fantastic job voicing Edward. I can’t recommend the audiobook enough.<br><br>I loved being in Edward Cullen’s head. Absolutely loved it. Yes, this is a <i>Twilight</i> retelling, but this is much longer than <i>Twilight</i> and so much was expanded on. I loved getting more from the Cullen’s and with Edward being able to read minds and all, you really did get to see more from so many of the other characters in this book. Plus just knowing Edward's side of things and what he was really thinking was truly a treat! I also have to say, I think Stephenie Meyer's writing has only gotten stronger with time. <br><br>If you’re a diehard fan of the Twilight Saga like me, I highly recommend giving this one a go! <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="15763710253844133084" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText1807761494216039855" style="display:none">Omg! THIS book was EVERYTHING! Please for the love of everything, Stephenie, write the rest of the books in Edward’s perspective!!! 🖤 I only put in a few quotes, but I will return with more at a later date!! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1596456231ra/29909952.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Holy shit snacks!! No trace of the shreds of humanity I’d managed to cloak myself in over the years remained. <br>I was a predator. She was my prey. There was nothing else in the whole world but that truth. <br><br>I was a vampire, and she had the sweetest blood I’d smelled in more than eighty years.</blockquote>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3479477346" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3479477346" />
    <a title="Nataliya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3672777-nataliya"><img alt="Nataliya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605995014p2/3672777.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3479477346?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nataliya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nataliya" href="/user/show/3672777-nataliya">Nataliya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/53333356-midnight-sun">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=2020-reads">2020-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3479477346" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16150316063184846958"><b>Pre-reading review:</b> Let’s be honest, I hated <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41865.Twilight__Twilight___1_' title='Twilight (Twilight, #1) by Stephenie Meyer' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twilight</a>. I *loved* hating <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41865.Twilight__Twilight___1_' title='Twilight (Twilight, #1) by Stephenie Meyer' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twilight</a>. Terrible as they were, those books had literary merits of a Twinkie - and were just as addicting. And now this is out, and can I really think I have the willpower not to read this sparkly creepy vampire opus? <br/><br/>Also, what the hell is that cover??? It’s seriously creepy. Pomegranate — or a partially dissected heart? Reminds me of anatomy lab and all that formaldehyde smell...<br/>—————<br/><b>Post-reading review:</b><br/><br/>Reader, I finished</span>
  <span id="freeText16150316063184846958" style="display:none"><b>Pre-reading review:</b> Let’s be honest, I hated <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41865.Twilight__Twilight___1_" title="Twilight (Twilight, #1) by Stephenie Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Twilight</a>. I *loved* hating <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41865.Twilight__Twilight___1_" title="Twilight (Twilight, #1) by Stephenie Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Twilight</a>. Terrible as they were, those books had literary merits of a Twinkie - and were just as addicting. And now this is out, and can I really think I have the willpower not to read this sparkly creepy vampire opus? <br><br>Also, what the hell is that cover??? It’s seriously creepy. Pomegranate — or a partially dissected heart? Reminds me of anatomy lab and all that formaldehyde smell...<br>—————<br><b>Post-reading review:</b><br><br>Reader, I finished it. <b>Yes, the entire 700+ pages</b>. That’s some self-discipline, mixed with masochism, apparently. <br><br>700+ pages of the story of the first <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41865.Twilight__Twilight___1_" title="Twilight (Twilight, #1) by Stephenie Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Twilight</a> book, told through Edward Sparklepire’s eyes. 700+ pages of overly-wordy, painfully bloated overwritten narration that does not dare skip ever the most insignificant detail or word. <b>700+ pages of self-loathing angst and cringeworthy romance basically told in real time.</b><br><blockquote> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1597002422i/29940801.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>But hey, I can sum up the first third of this magnum opus pretty succinctly, courtesy of RiffTrax guys and <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=SE0fknMFFXg" rel="nofollow noopener">their bloodthirsty 40-second parody version of Edward’s lullaby with these immortal lyrics</a> <i>(lullaby because the creepy stalker Sparkleson climbs into her room through the window every night and without her knowledge or consent obsessively for hours on end watches her sleep. Blergh):</i><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380223841i/681094.jpg" width="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>
  <br>
  <i>"I want to chomp into your throoooooat.<br>And watch you bleed out on the floooooor.<br>Then I'll bathe myself in your life essence as you die.<br>Tear your heart out of your chest <br>and crack the bones <br>and suck the marrow out. <br>Slice into your brain for sandwiches <br>and maybe have an omelette made of--"</i>
</blockquote><br>We already knew that cute subtle sparkly sheen was the skin of a killer. We knew Edward Sparklemeister was an angsty broody uptight guy with serious control issues and obsessive creepy stalker/ abusive boyfriend personality. <b>What I don’t think I realized before is how petty and judgmental Sparklepants actually was</b>. Literally the opening scene of this book has his internal monologue bitch and whine about everyone and everything around him, including his family. <br><blockquote>
<i> “Why did she have to come here? Why did she have to exist? Why did she have to ruin the little peace I had in this nonlife of mine? Why had this aggravating human ever been born? She would ruin me.”</i><br><br>(Also, <a href="https://web.archive.org/web/20170721091133/https://balcarin.livejournal.com/462027.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Growing Up Cullen</a>, ultimate genius. Read and rejoice - it captures Edward’s character perfectly) </blockquote><br>This book is much MUCH longer than Twilight - probably because in addition to <b>Edward’s incessant self-loathing inner monologue</b> we also get, via his eavesdropping mind-reading ability, constant recaps of Bella’s conversations with other characters. And *everything* that those characters thought, in strangely coherent sentences.<br><blockquote> Reading looong sections of Edward eavesdropping on other people’s thoughts made me finally realize what bugs me about this whole setup: people don’t spend their whole day running their internal monologues in perfectly coherent sentences, like a book. At least I don’t. It would be a jumble of images, sentence fragments, overlapping distracted thoughts, visuals, etc. That can’t be just me, right?</blockquote><br>It’s the sheer number of details. About everything. Obsessively. <b>Every minute detail. Every single word ever said. </b>Twenty pages of Edward interrogating Bella about her likes and dislikes. A page and a half of Sparkly Sparkleson choosing a shirt to wear. An hour of reading dialogue describing everything from Bella’s favorite color to favorite bands to favorite books to her favorite ... <i>*SNORE*</i> Pardon me, I must have dozed off from boredom here. Sufficient to say that <b>pacing — what pacing?</b><br><blockquote> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1597002422i/29940802._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br><b>My best guess is that this book is supposed to serve as a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41865.Twilight__Twilight___1_" title="Twilight (Twilight, #1) by Stephenie Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Twilight</a> encyclopedia / retcon. </b><br><br>- <i>Was Bella’s character criticized as an empty self-insert shell of a person in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41865.Twilight__Twilight___1_" title="Twilight (Twilight, #1) by Stephenie Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Twilight</a>?</i> No problem, let’s cram every single detail about her here to refute that.<br><blockquote>
  <i> “There was a bit of Jane Eyre in her, a portion of Scout Finch and Jo March, a measure of Elinor Dashwood, and Lucy Pevensie.”</i>
</blockquote><br>- <i>Was Bella criticized for being too self-absorbed and judgmental towards other non-vampire characters in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41865.Twilight__Twilight___1_" title="Twilight (Twilight, #1) by Stephenie Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Twilight</a>? </i>No problem, let’s make sure that every character surrounding her here thinks such a barrage of vile thoughts at her that by contrast she appears to be Heaven incarnate and <b>shines like a judgmental petty diamond she is.</b><br><blockquote>
  <i> “The English language needed a word that meant something halfway between a goddess and a naiad.”</i>
</blockquote><br>- <i>Was Edward criticized for angry and abusive stalkerish behavior in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41865.Twilight__Twilight___1_" title="Twilight (Twilight, #1) by Stephenie Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Twilight</a>?</i> No problem, let’s just insert a billion justifications about how he totally respects Bella’s choices and how what would seem to be controlling and stalkerish behavior totally isn’t, and <b>he sparkles like a judgmental prissy diamond he is. </b>Except when the creepy is still there (since Meyer wrote it twice already):<br><blockquote>
  <i> “And then she started to walk away from me.<br>Without thinking about my action, I automatically reached out and caught her by the back of her rain jacket. She jerked to a stop.<br>“Where do you think you’re going?” I was upset—almost angry that she was leaving. I hadn’t had enough time with her.”</i>
</blockquote><br><blockquote> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1597002422i/29940803._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>And the language. Oh, the Bella-levels clumsy language (<i>“her heart throbbed wetly just a foot from my ear”</i>) and overwrought descriptions (<i>“Her scent hit me like a battering ram, like an exploding grenade”</i>) and clunky metaphors (<i>“The electricity ricocheted around the inside of my stomach”, “my voice wrapped around her name like a caress”</i>).<br><br><b>Enjoy the highlights reel:</b><br><blockquote>
  <i>“She was from a much brighter, warmer place—her skin seemed to reflect that somehow, despite its fairness—and the cold must make her uncomfortable.”</i>
</blockquote><br>Her skin reflects no such thing. Apparently she’s corpse-like in her translucent paleness and you keep emphasizing how translucently pale she is. Eddykins, you are just making sh*t up now.<br>—————<blockquote>
  <i>“I smiled at the threat, then gently kissed her again, quitting as soon as her heart started acting up.”<br><br>“Her heartbeat thudded louder than before, and the rhythm was abruptly staccato.”</i>
</blockquote><br>Holy crow, as Bella would say. Sparkleson, your actions seem to trigger some serious arrhythmia in your girlfriend. You may want to think about EKG. Two medical degrees, Doctor Sparklepants — you know this could be deadly.<br>——————<blockquote> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1597002422i/29940804._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>- A few times hopelessly smitten women literally think <i>“Swoon”</i> when ogling the marble Adonis that Edward is. How often do you see an attractive person and proceed to actually verbalize in your head, <i>“Swoon”</i>? I never have - but maybe I way too busy actually swooning rather than thinking <i>“Swoon”?</i> (Also, “swoon” no longer seems like a real word).<br>—————<blockquote>
  <i>“I fall down a lot when I run,” she said sheepishly.”</i>
</blockquote> <br>What the hell IS wrong with Bella? Those balance and coordination issues are way more than endearing clumsiness. Did she have a stroke? Does she have a brain tumor? I mean, a person should be able to walk on a flat surface without tripping for at least a few steps, right? Did you say TWO medical degrees, Dr. Sparkletoes? You never considered asking your girlfriend to get a brain MRI?<br>——————<blockquote>
  <i>“I stared at her in blank surprise. “People can’t smell blood.”</i>
</blockquote><br>Stephenie Meyer doesn’t know how human sense of smell works. Or maybe I’m a vampire, too.<br>——————<blockquote>
  <i>“She waited in silence, her teeth pressing into her soft lower lip.<br>That sight distracted me for a second. Strange, unfamiliar reactions stirred deep in my forgotten human core.”</i>
</blockquote><br>Dear Edward Sparklepants. Strange unfamiliar reactions deep in your core? Don’t you have two medical degrees and a lifetime spent in biology classes? I know you’re a 100-year-old virgin, but you must understand, no? It’s arousal, buddy. You are simply horny.<br>——————<br>——————<br><br><b>Anyway, you get the gist.<br><br>Now I’m hoping that Meyer does not decide to rewrite the rest of the books from other POVs. <br><br>Oh crap, I hope I haven’t given her any ideas....</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="16150316063184846958" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="• Lindsey Dahling •" class="user" itemprop="url" name="• Lindsey Dahling •" href="/user/show/26262267-lindsey-dahling">• Lindsey Dahling •</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3319776363" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11065428414641817358">Look, I’m doing this for high school Lindsey. She had to suffer through the low-rise jeans phase, so I owe it to her.<br/><br/>Even though she and I will NEVER be cool with Bella’s floor-length khaki skirt.<br/><br/>————————————————————————<br/><b>Update:</b> DNF at 34%<br/><br/>Look, I can’t do this even for low-rise jeans high school Lindsey. <br/><br/>I’d like to say she’d understand, but the day Stephenie Meyer posted the leaked chapters on her website, high school Lindsey drove to the public library after school just to read them. And she lo</span>
  <span id="freeText11065428414641817358" style="display:none">Look, I’m doing this for high school Lindsey. She had to suffer through the low-rise jeans phase, so I owe it to her.<br /><br />Even though she and I will NEVER be cool with Bella’s floor-length khaki skirt.<br /><br />————————————————————————<br /><b>Update:</b> DNF at 34%<br /><br />Look, I can’t do this even for low-rise jeans high school Lindsey. <br /><br />I’d like to say she’d understand, but the day Stephenie Meyer posted the leaked chapters on her website, high school Lindsey drove to the public library after school just to read them. And she loved them.<br /><br />High school Lindsey was a moron.<br /><br />Edward’s POV adds nothing new to the story. It’s mainly just him going on and on and on and on about every little thing. So much so that I, an annoying AF over-thinker, couldn’t tolerate it. Bella may be one-dimensional, but at least she knows how to move the plot along. Edward is incapable of doing so. <br /><br />Also, a lot of the dialogue didn’t really make sense from his POV. It’s almost as if Stephenie Meyer was writing all of these inner monologues for Edward and then remembered she needed to include the dialogue from the first book, so she just plopped it in random places. None of his thoughts are snarky or amused, but his dialogue certainly is. The two don’t match. And yes, yes, I’m aware not everyone says what’s they’re thinking. But, there were parts in Twilight where he seemed genuinely amused by Bella. Yet, none of his thoughts reflect that. Thus, it feels patched together.<br /><br />Really a shame this didn’t come out 14 years ago. High school Lindsey would already own a pillow case of the cover. As it is, present day Lindsey is still suffering from the effects low rise jeans had on my hips, SO I AM NOT EVEN SORRY FOR QUITTING THIS.</span>

<div id="review_3480483129" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3480483129" />
    <a title="Nilufer Ozmekik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik"><img alt="Nilufer Ozmekik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559807601p2/53701594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3480483129?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nilufer Ozmekik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nilufer Ozmekik" href="/user/show/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik">Nilufer Ozmekik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3480483129" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3861703314350926889">I’m swimming at the complex feelings sea, keeping my head above as forming thought balloons. I wish I read this book 10 years ago. It should have been released as soon as the trilogy has ended so I could have given my five shiny stars because this book is definitely written better, bringing out more clear perspective to the characters’ stories, their motives. But it is still flawed and there are still plot holes, logical mistakes. <br/><br/>But right now, everything has changed: my taste of music, food, l</span>
  <span id="freeText3861703314350926889" style="display:none">I’m swimming at the complex feelings sea, keeping my head above as forming thought balloons. I wish I read this book 10 years ago. It should have been released as soon as the trilogy has ended so I could have given my five shiny stars because this book is definitely written better, bringing out more clear perspective to the characters’ stories, their motives. But it is still flawed and there are still plot holes, logical mistakes. <br /><br />But right now, everything has changed: my taste of music, food, literature, movies completely evolved. In last 15 years I became vegetarian, yoga instructor and cut the alcohol, meditating daily, supporting Republicans. Okay, I take them back. Especially the part about my political choices ( don’t worry I didn’t lose every marbles in my head. It was my coldest joke. After writing it, I’m still shivering!) <br /><br />I didn’t radically changed but I’m not in my twenties anymore and I am not fan girl of Edward Cullen. Now I’m in my forties and I’m fan of new Batman. (See, my tastes are already evolved. I’m not obsessed with blonde, charming Brit and I don’t cry each time Cedric Diggory dies when I watch Harry Potter and Goblet of Fire! Okay, this is another lie! Of course I’m crying! )<br /><br />I have to admit this book is great contribution to the series and writing still is obviously so much better. I truly loved to be inside of Edward Cullen’s head and it already filled so many blank points about him and Bella’s story. <br /><br />He is not perfect. He is tormented by his inner feelings: animal inside of him tries to slake his thirst. And his human parts start to discover Bella’s attributes which help us look from the different mirror to the character and understand how she is so unique. ( Actually we also learn more about her high school friends who were mostly hatable! I really question author’s reasoning to create those irritating friends group reminded you of cheesy 80’s thriller movie characters who were extremely stupid and became first ones to die! Maybe their only contribution was emphasizing Bella’s incredibly perfect attributes!!! )<br /><br />And I’m still lost why Edward deeply fell in love with Bella. It is still instant, too quick. <br /><br />The pacing is good but it is still too much wordy. If I haven’t been inside one of my favorite characters’ head, I would scream him shut the hell up and tell me his shorter version of the story.<br /><br />And of course we already know the entire story. So there is no surprising element! (Edward could have killed Bella, imprinted on Jacob which would be my all time favorite alternative final!) So we keep living deja vu, time traveling, remembering our past reading journey over and over again. <br /><br />But this book reminded me of how much I liked Emmet and Alice as supporting characters and I’m so happy to spend longer time with them. <br /><br />So it is belated meeting and back to past, tribute to one of the most popular trilogy kind of reading for me. I wish I wouldn’t take so much time to come out and I wish it could be a little shorter. I didn’t fall in love with it but I didn’t unlike it. It’s a solid three starred read for me. I had fun to go back and meet with the characters, rekindling my memories. But that’s all. Unfortunately this is not extremely exciting, earth shattering experience for me.<br /><br /><a href="https://niluferozmekik.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/nilylovestoread/" rel="nofollow noopener">instagram</a><br /><a href="https://www.facebook.com/nilufer.ozmekik" rel="nofollow noopener">facebook</a><br /><a href="https://twitter.com/NiluferOzmekik" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3861703314350926889" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3542891179" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3542891179" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3542891179?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781549134661" href="/book/show/53288277-midnight-sun">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=libby-app">libby-app</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3542891179" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5827168319718269926"><b>I loved Twilight. Fuck <i>all</i> y'all haters. </b><br/>I've been salivating to read this ever since that partial first draft of the original Midnight Sun got leaked <i>years</i> ago.<br/><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1600786885ra/30139457.gif' width='400' height='220' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>But after reading <i>this</i>? I wish Stephenie Meyer had just pulled on her big girl panties and finished it <i>back then. </i><br/><b>This</b> Edward was too breathy and overdramatic. He came across as one of those sensitive men who would willingly saw his penis off as an apology for <i>scaring</i> you with his boner.<br/>Getthefuckoutofhere.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1600787388ra/30139469.gif' width='400' height='180' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The first few chapters were th</span>
  <span id="freeText5827168319718269926" style="display:none"><b>I loved Twilight. Fuck <i>all</i> y'all haters. </b><br>I've been salivating to read this ever since that partial first draft of the original Midnight Sun got leaked <i>years</i> ago.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1600786885ra/30139457.gif" width="400" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But after reading <i>this</i>? I wish Stephenie Meyer had just pulled on her big girl panties and finished it <i>back then. </i><br><b>This</b> Edward was too breathy and overdramatic. He came across as one of those sensitive men who would willingly saw his penis off as an apology for <i>scaring</i> you with his boner.<br>Getthefuckoutofhere.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1600787388ra/30139469.gif" width="400" height="180" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The first few chapters were the hardest, because Edward sounded like such a poncy twat that I really didn't know if I wanted to keep listening to his inner monologue. He was so condescending and obnoxious, it just felt like his thoughts were on a repetitive loop. <br><b>I am a Vampyre! Humans are Gross!</b><br>That schtick that got old. Fast.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1599943776ra/30098328.gif" width="400" height="180" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'll admit that as the story went on, he really did become a lot more tolerable.<br>Gotta be honest though, he was <i>not</i> as charming as I remembered. One (petty) reason is most likely because I imagined this super hot guy when I read the book a million years ago. I can't remember what that dream man looked like now, however, because I have an image of Pattinson stuck in my head. This is <i>not</i> the image I wanted. <br>The guy who played Edward is one of those rare people who has two faces. I'll look at him from one angle and think, <i>Hey! He's not half bad!</i><br>Then he tilts his head a bit to the left? <b>Jesus Christ! It's a monster!</b> <br>That's a skill an actor can use right there.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1600377945ra/30120343.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Anyway. The whole book was probably a bit marred by those terrible movies and the actors who played the roles. What did they do to make them look that way - paint them with chalk each day on the set? They were supposed to be pale and attractive, not look like they'd been dipped in white-out. <br><b>And can someone please explain why half the time they look like they're wearing cheap wigs!?</b><br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1600789330ra/30139588.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Ugh.<br>I can't know for sure how much my loathing for those movies <i>did</i> to taint my viewpoint, but I<i> do know</i> that I preferred the characters that I'd imagined a long time ago more than what I kept seeing this time around.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1600380026ra/30120411.gif" width="400" height="160" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Alright. I get it. This is supposed to be a representation of how you feel in the throes of your first love. But I honestly don't remember being <i>this</i> fucking dramatic. Maybe I was. I'm willing to admit that I may have forgotten what it was like to think of a man as the all-encompassing center of my universe. Yeah, yeah. I love my husband...but not like <i>this</i>. This is just a lot of teenage nonsense. They're both virgins who have never been in love (or even dated anyone) beforehand. <br><b>You remember what that was like, right?<br><i>Yeah. Me neither.</i></b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1600379580ra/30120405.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br>And that's ok. It's part of what's so fun about occasionally dipping my toes back into the Young Adult genre. You're giving yourself permission to forget reality and pretend that breathy sighs, chaste kisses, and holding hands are what makes the world go round. You can believe that your love for this <i>perfect</i> boy will make up for the fact that his family are all raging lunatics that you'll be tethered to till the end of time. &lt;--it's all good.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1600788600ra/30139541.gif" width="400" height="180" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>At any rate, I finished this for nostalgia's sake. But I can't say that it recaptured any of that original magic I felt when I first read the books. <br>But I'm a glutton for punishment, so if she makes a New Moon version from Ed's point of view?<br>Yeah. I'll read that bitch. &lt;--not even ashamed!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5827168319718269926" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3317849398" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3317849398" />
    <a title="✨ A ✨ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/65321843-a"><img alt="✨ A ✨ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604503440p2/65321843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3317849398?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨ A ✨ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨ A ✨ " href="/user/show/65321843-a">✨ A ✨ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/53329548-midnight-sun">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=2020-release">2020-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=three-and-half-stars">three-and-half-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3317849398" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6410454437208547173">It takes another kind of genius to <b>sell us the same story three times and still get us hyped up for it.</b><br/><br/><i>Twilight</i> has it's flaws. This we know. This we acknowledge. It's like one of those low budget soap operas. You know it's terrible shit, but you also can't stop yourself from watching the next episode. <br/><br/>Well that's how it is <i>for me</i> anyway. <br/><br/>If you're thinking of picking this up please know that it's basically the <b>exact same</b> story as <i>Twilight</i> (book 1) with a few added parts since (unbelievably) Edw</span>
  <span id="freeText6410454437208547173" style="display:none">It takes another kind of genius to <b>sell us the same story three times and still get us hyped up for it.</b><br /><br /><i>Twilight</i> has it's flaws. This we know. This we acknowledge. It's like one of those low budget soap operas. You know it's terrible shit, but you also can't stop yourself from watching the next episode. <br /><br />Well that's how it is <i>for me</i> anyway. <br /><br />If you're thinking of picking this up please know that it's basically the <b>exact same</b> story as <i>Twilight</i> (book 1) with a few added parts since (unbelievably) Edward is not always glued to Bella's side. <br /><br />Even though this book took me ages to read, I laughed at all the cringey scenes <b>but also thoroughly enjoyed myself.</b> I got a tad bit annoyed at the sense of deja vu but then again I've read and reread this series waaaaayy more times than I'd like to admit. <br /><br /><br />I always used to think of <b>Bella as having a personality of a potato</b>. But I kind of get her ‘allure’ to Edward now. Edward is very perceptive and I liked the things he noticed about Bella's character. The way he is able to read minds and NOT able read Bella's mind means that he picked up on all her little quirks and sees her in a different light than she sees herself. <b>He actually made me like her</b>. *GASP* I honestly cannot believe I just wrote that. <br /><br />I've also always been hardcore #TeamJacob (don't come at me for that) but reading from Edwards POV has nudged me just a tiny bit to the other side. He's <b>more real than he appeared in the other books</b>. I loved reading about his inner turmoil and the way he justifies his crazy actions. However the dude is still a creepy stalker ( #TeamJacob4evaaaaa).<br /><br />In <i>Midnight Sun</i> we not only get Edward's POV but also his insight and the thoughts he reads through other people's minds. Which was fascinating!! I honestly don't know how he stays sane. Learning more about Edward, Alice and Jasper's powers/abilities was so cool.<br /><br />I loved the flashbacks. We got to know more about Edwards early days, more about Carlisle, how Alice and Jasper joined the family and other fun stuff! <br /><br />Bella is an outsider looking in to the Cullen crew. But <b>Edward's perspective as a member of the family was precious</b>. Those were some of my favourite parts of this book. <br /><br />Rosalie is one of my favourite characters. Yes, she's a bitch. But I love it. The more in depth version of how she found Emmet had me almost in tears (okay that's a lie. I <i>was</i> in tears). It was beautiful. <br /><br />Every single time Edward referred to ‘the monster inside me’ . It was just so cringe. And it happened so often I started laughing everytime he said it. <br /><br /><br /><br /><u>
  <b>Final thoughts:</b>
</u><br /><br />It would have been better if <i>Twilight</i> was first written with alternating POV from both Bella and Edward. <b>Is this book a necessary read? Definitely not.</b> But I'm glad I read it. It's for those of us with a sentimental attachment to these books and these characters, those of us who have been waiting years for Edward's side of the story.<br /><br />I highly recommend the audiobook. The best part of this whole experience was having Jake Abel and his beautiful voice in my head for hours (I swear that sounded less creepy in my head. clearly Edward's creep vibes have been rubbing off on me). He did a phenomenal job at narrating. ✨ <br /><br /><b>3.5 stars <br /><br />[I think pomegranates can be sexy however THAT pomegranate is not it, just saying.]</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="6410454437208547173" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3522733468?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whitney Atkinson" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson">Whitney Atkinson</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3522733468" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3962584971462261765">this was the most bizarre mix of returning to childhood while also having that childhood ruined. it really put a damper on twilight's barely tolerable creepiness to learn that even when edward isn't noticeably with bella, he's always lurking in a tree outside her house or something. a book i thought would take me a weekend to devour ended up taking 3 weeks, so let that struggle speak for itself.<br/><br/>(random sidenote: one thing i didn't expect from this was how much more i came to love emmett)</span>

          </span>
        </div>
