<div id="review_3480073749" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3480073749" />
    <a title="Bookishrealm" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27544898-bookishrealm"><img alt="Bookishrealm" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460563618p2/27544898.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3480073749?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bookishrealm" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bookishrealm" href="/user/show/27544898-bookishrealm">Bookishrealm</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27544898-bookishrealm?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27544898-bookishrealm?shelf=ya-paranormal">ya-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27544898-bookishrealm?shelf=books-read-in-2020">books-read-in-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3480073749" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14673706471344079100"><b>If I could give this 1/2 star I would, but you know the way the rating system works on Goodreads...This is ain't it folks. This really didn't do anything for me.</b><br/><br/>If you know me or if you've been following my journey in re-reading the Twilight series then you know that I have not been enjoying any of these books. It's been a rough journey, but has also given me better insight to understanding why and how this series is problematic. I won't lie; I was curious about how Meyer would frame this book i</span>
  <span id="freeText14673706471344079100" style="display:none"><b>If I could give this 1/2 star I would, but you know the way the rating system works on Goodreads...This is ain't it folks. This really didn't do anything for me.</b><br /><br />If you know me or if you've been following my journey in re-reading the Twilight series then you know that I have not been enjoying any of these books. It's been a rough journey, but has also given me better insight to understanding why and how this series is problematic. I won't lie; I was curious about how Meyer would frame this book in context of the original book. My curiosity wasn't enough to even begin to make me like this book. <br /><br />Let's get the easy part of this out of the way. <i>Midnight Sun</i> is boring. I know everyone was/is super excited to see Twilight from Edwards perspective; however, there was no reason for this book to be over 600 pages. We literally revisit every scene word for word with Edwards insight tacked on. By the time I was 50% into the book it began to feel very long and drawn out. Her technical writing skills have improved; however, her ability to write a compelling plot has not changed. Would it have been a better book if it was shorter? For me, probably not because the content itself is still problematic; however, I think it would have been an easier read. An interesting part of this book is that Stephenie Meyer essentially attempts to re-write the book in a way that attempts to get rid of the critiques that she experienced with the first four books. In doing this, she recreates characters that aren't true to the source material which was WEIRD. For example, I thought Bella was a bland, boring, and insensitive character in Twilight. In <i>Midnight Sun</i> she becomes this well rounded, interesting, and compassionate character. I'm not sure if she was attempting to paint this picture that Edward was seeing Bella through rose-colored glasses, but it didn't make sense. There were also scenes in Twilight that were incorrectly translated over to Midnight Sun as if Meyer didn't even attempt to re-read her own work before writing <i>Midnight Sun</i>. <br /><br />Now....what I can't seem to understand is how 10 years later Meyer still has the monopoly of writing problematic crap. I feel like she attempted to keep the Black family out of this book as much as possible because she received so much backlash for her portrayal of the Quileute tribe. She still couldn't get it right. There was a line in the beginning of the book in which Meyer allowed Edward to say that he had no problem SLAUGHTERING the entire Quileute tribe because he felt that Jacob broke their treaty. First, the imagery that this brings to mind is disgusting. Second, think about the fact that it is a White character saying this. I don't think that this was appropriate in any world to write that line. Then there is the issue with Edward acknowledging that he is no better than a peeping Tom and that he's a stalker, but continues to stalk her anyway. It's almost as if Meyer believed that if she acknowledged the behavior then she wouldn't have to fix it. There was also this weird alignment with God and Carlise. Don't get me wrong Carlise is hands down one of my favorite characters; however, I found it very awkward that she had Edward describe Carlise as this a Christ-like figure. It was clear that she still wanted to make sure that she wrote herself and her beliefs into the book. There is still a whole aspect of control on Edwards part and the inability of women to be able to define their own lives. I feel like Meyer intentionally wrote all of the other high school students as villains so that should justify the isolation that ends up occurring between Edward and Bella. I just didn't feel comfortable with a lot of the contents of the book. <br /><br />There were a few things that I did like about the book including the scenes where we learned more about the Cullens and some of the back story about the final scene. Was it enough to save the book? No. Will I be reading anything else in the future? No. I appreciated having open and candid conversations about these books, but I think, for me, it's time to close the door on this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14673706471344079100" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

At one point in my life, I liked Twilight then when re-reading I could not believe what I saw in those books. But despite all that, Twilight definitely brought a change to the book scene. <span id="freeTextContainer16672944885804286067"><b>I finally finished Midnight Sun, so here is a compiled list of my Thoughts™</b><br/><br/>* most days I can hardly muster 3 words to describe my overall existence, but my boy Edward here spends pages describing how Bella’s eyes react to the light and let me tell you, that shit is lit 👏😂<br/><br/>* <i>“A word I’d never said before in the presence of a lady slid between my clenched teeth.”</i> - Edward, honey, it’s fine, you can say fuck 🤣<br/><br/>* Edward Cullen falling for someone - a reaction in 5 steps:<br/> - shout NO dramatically in fro</span>
  <span id="freeText16672944885804286067" style="display:none"><b>I finally finished Midnight Sun, so here is a compiled list of my Thoughts™</b><br /><br />* most days I can hardly muster 3 words to describe my overall existence, but my boy Edward here spends pages describing how Bella’s eyes react to the light and let me tell you, that shit is lit 👏😂<br /><br />* <i>“A word I’d never said before in the presence of a lady slid between my clenched teeth.”</i> - Edward, honey, it’s fine, you can say fuck 🤣<br /><br />* Edward Cullen falling for someone - a reaction in 5 steps:<br /> - shout NO dramatically in front of your family<br /> - view this as a <i>“destruction of my life”</i> and a <i>“mutilation of my future”</i><br /> - stalk out dramatically out of the house, into the rain<br /> - writhe internally in agony<br /> - run through the mountains, in the rain, contemplating your existence, like the dramatic queen that you are<br /><br />* <i>“High school. Purgatory no longer, it was now purely hell. Torment and fire… yes, I had both.”</i> - I dare y'all to name a more dramatic, over the top bitch than Edward “my life is agony” Cullen<br /><br />* Edward Cullen discovering jealousy: <i>“I didn’t understand this emotion - it was such a tangle of pain and fury and desire and despair. I had never felt it before; I couldn’t put a name to it.”</i> - yes boo, welcome to the highs and lows of Feelings™<br /><br />* <i>“Suddenly, as she ate, a strange comparison entered my head. For just a second, I saw Persephone, pomegranate in hand. Dooming herself to the underworld. Is that who i was? Hades himself, coveting springtime, stealing it, condemning it to endless night.”</i> - name 👏 a 👏 more 👏 dramatic 👏 bitch 👏<br /><br />* Edward’s idea of a “state of undress” is wearing a short sleeved shirt, i’m howling; for real, he is in mental anguish over wearing that shit<br /><br />* <i>“I swallowed Bella’s tear. Perhaps it would never leave my body. After she left me, after all the lonely years had passed, maybe I would always have this piece of her inside me.”</i> - Edward, honey, I like you boo, but what the FUCK<br /><br />* Edward literally decided to think all the thoughts and use all the words in the dictionary. All of them. Just… why the fuck not<br /><br />* Emmett is the one reason to give this book a try. He constantly calls Edward kid. His general attitude towards everything is a flip between yolo and “can i murder that”. He’s basically like “edward, man, you’re fucking weird, but i’m bored, so let’s do this, i guess”<br /><br />*<i> “there are other hungers, I continued. Hungers I don’t even understand, that are foreign to me”</i> - a Very Dramatic way of saying that you’re horny, courtesy of Edward “my mind is impure” Cullen<br /><br />* this book had NO business being as long as it was, but it was peak nostalgia™ and i loved every second of it<br /><br />* at the same time, i swear to fuck, i don’t think i’ll ever reread it, edward’s mind is an exhausting place to live in lmao</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3318281917" />
    <a title="lazybookconqueror" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/101933148-lazybookconqueror"><img alt="lazybookconqueror" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567020969p2/101933148.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3318281917?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="lazybookconqueror" class="user" itemprop="url" name="lazybookconqueror" href="/user/show/101933148-lazybookconqueror">lazybookconqueror</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/53328856-midnight-sun">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/101933148-lazybookconqueror?shelf=2020books">2020books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/101933148-lazybookconqueror?shelf=highly-anticipated">highly-anticipated</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3318281917" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14865496082434786619">This was honestly a lot better than I expected it to be. Yes, it might be the nostalgia talking, but it wasn't as cringy as I thought it would and it definitely gave us more insight to the Cullen family, especially the relationship between Alice and Edward, and that was cool.<br/><br/>Is this a masterpiece? Definitely no. And I'm not sure how interesting this would be for people who aren't fans of the original books. But, to me, it was a lovely walk down memory lane. Even with all the brooding.<br/><br/>-----------</span>
  <span id="freeText14865496082434786619" style="display:none">This was honestly a lot better than I expected it to be. Yes, it might be the nostalgia talking, but it wasn't as cringy as I thought it would and it definitely gave us more insight to the Cullen family, especially the relationship between Alice and Edward, and that was cool.<br><br>Is this a masterpiece? Definitely no. And I'm not sure how interesting this would be for people who aren't fans of the original books. But, to me, it was a lovely walk down memory lane. Even with all the brooding.<br><br>-------------------------------------------------------------------<br><br>Previous update.<br><br>THIS IS HAPPENING. My inner teen is *screaming* and I'm here for it. #sorrynotsorry<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1479564297ra/21207394.gif" width="480" height="197" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

And tbh every other girl I know is the same !! sooo we are like each other!!<br>NO SUCH THING AS "NOT LIKE OTHER GURLLLLLLS" !!!<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1605294358i/30374267._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1605294358i/30374268._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1605294358i/30374269._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I mean it got soooooo repetitive !! And Edys pov wasn't even interesting !!<br>So I kinda get why he might like her<br>BOTH THINK they are special snowflake<br>LUCKILY I did not read Bella's POV..cause I think it would have been even traumatizing<br>Just gonna stop here cause not much to say<br><b>NOTE: I DONOT intend to make fun of anyone who liked this series..It wasn't for ME. My problem was with the book NOT the author or readers who enjoyed this. I hope no one takes this personally😊🤗</b><br>Kinda Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/68964075-rue" rel="nofollow noopener">The one who went MIA</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52474875-mari" rel="nofollow noopener">The one who tried her best to keep this be going</a> AND OFC <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/63414753-tani" rel="nofollow noopener">The one who dragged us all into this mess</a><br><br><br><b>Update 3</b><br>Lets start with a diagram...<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1597767063i/29984845._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>W1=Window no.1<br>W2=Window no.2<br>BS= book shelf<br>That weird thing in the corner=Door<br><br>Special mentions<br>Bookshelf(duh)<br>Kitchen..which is accessible through the door(kitchen is imp..its keeps me well fed)<br>Mrin=Thats me saying "Hii" to you guys<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1597767063i/29984846._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now before reading Midnight Sun..<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1597767063i/29984844._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Mrin NOT afraid of windows..having a peaceful sleep<br><br>After reading it..<br>terrified of windows<br>You see..I have <b>TWO</b> HUGE windows &amp;               <span id="reviewTextContainer3479807218" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2556142864486319370">Five stars purely for the nostalgia value. It made me want to go back and read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41865.Twilight__Twilight___1_' title='Twilight (Twilight, #1) by Stephenie Meyer' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twilight</a> again. Or even watch the movie!<br/><br/>Of course the first section we have read before, back in the day, when the leaking of her manuscript caused such a sensation and made Meyer throw the book into the back of a cupboard. The middle section suited me perfectly because my favourite parts were always the Cullens at home and there was lots of that. Many other things became clearer too. How Alice's gift works. How Edwar</span>
  <span id="freeText2556142864486319370" style="display:none">Five stars purely for the nostalgia value. It made me want to go back and read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41865.Twilight__Twilight___1_" title="Twilight (Twilight, #1) by Stephenie Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Twilight</a> again. Or even watch the movie!<br /><br />Of course the first section we have read before, back in the day, when the leaking of her manuscript caused such a sensation and made Meyer throw the book into the back of a cupboard. The middle section suited me perfectly because my favourite parts were always the Cullens at home and there was lots of that. Many other things became clearer too. How Alice's gift works. How Edward was able to use Alice's gift to advantage. Jasper's gift was described fully and it explained why he glowered so much in the movie. <br /><br />Best of all though was the final part, especially the back story to the scene with James in the dance studio. In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41865.Twilight__Twilight___1_" title="Twilight (Twilight, #1) by Stephenie Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Twilight</a> we were horrified by Bella's situation and then suddenly Edward and the team popped up to save her. In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/53287484.Midnight_Sun__Twilight___5_" title="Midnight Sun (Twilight, #5) by Stephenie Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Midnight Sun</a> we get to see how the rescue actually eventuated and all the details of how it was covered up afterwards. Alice shows herself to be one formidable vampire, but then we already knew that.<br /><br />And then the ending with its sad undertones and a much better understanding of Edward's emotions which we know will lead to all those blank pages in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/49041.New_Moon__Twilight___2_" title="New Moon (Twilight, #2) by Stephenie Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">New Moon</a>. <br /><br />I thought this was totally worth reading but ONLY if you are already a fan.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2556142864486319370" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4ceMyGs4U1tyAew9s+RgxIuf4UlniHZrYS6iTWJ+pNrHBv179JqEaBCX7XxNVqs155hM/QILAcBaoMVxGSbzFQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('N9Q1ir/G9TmCX7QAevxXVghr2zRubmR9vjfuDlSlbN0RFUQ5IGQiCuDJtUGETpynZGx2gAvtE9aFuYkyL/07Eg==')})
  }

  <span id="freeText11317849344838799653" style="display:none">Stephenie Meyer is the author of the bestselling <i>Twilight</i> series, <i>The Host</i>, and <i>The Chemist</i>. <i>Twilight</i> was one of 2005's most talked about novels and within weeks of its release the book debuted at #5 on The New York Times bestseller list. Among its many accolades, <i>Twilight</i> was named an "ALA Top Ten Books for Young Adults," an Amazon.com "Best Book of the Decade So Far," and a Publishers Weekly Best Book of the Year. <br /><br />Meyer graduated from Brigham Young University with a degree in English Literature. She lives in Arizona with her husband and three sons.</span>
